[3:5:344,489] disabilities. These services are provided to  

[4:0:344,499] California's residents, including vulnerable and at-

[4:1:344,509] risk children and adults, in ways that promote  

[4:2:344,519] health and well-being, strengthen and preserve  

[4:3:344,529] families, encourage personal responsibility, and  

[4:4:344,539] foster independence.

[2:3:66,141] 3810 - REGIONAL OFFICES AND REGIONAL ADVISORY COMMITTEES  

[3:0:66,162] Twelve Regional Offices and Regional Advisory Committees provide administrative support and assist with advocacy, training,  

[3:1:66,172] coordination, and implementation of State Plan objectives in Council Regions throughout California. These offices and advisory  

[3:2:66,182] committees provide information and data to the Council to assess regional needs and implementation of the State Plan and for  

[3:3:66,192] inclusion in reports to the federal government and the Legislature.  

[4:0:66,213] In addition to implementation of State Plan activities, Regional Office staff support the following activities to improve and  

[4:1:66,223] enhance the availability and quality of services for residents of state developmental centers and state-operated community  

[4:2:66,233] facilities:  

[5:0:65,251] • Advocacy services through volunteers recruited by Council staff for individuals who have no legally appointed representative  

[5:1:76,261] to assist them in making choices and decisions.  

[5:2:65,277] • Clients' rights advocacy services to ensure that laws, regulations, and policies pertaining to the rights of persons with  

[5:3:76,287] developmental disabilities are observed.  

[5:4:65,304] • Quality Assessments for individuals who receive community residential services and support.

[5:0:66,194] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,213] 3820 - EMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICES AUTHORITY  

[6:1:66,231] Disaster Medical Services Division  

[7:0:66,249] The Disaster Medical Services Division coordinates California's medical response to major disasters by carrying out the  

[7:1:66,259] Authority's mandate to provide medical resources to local governments in support of their disaster response efforts. The  

[7:2:66,269] Division coordinates with the Governor's Office of Emergency Services, the Office of Homeland Security, the California National  

[7:3:66,279] Guard, the California Department of Public Health, and other local, state, and federal agencies, private sector hospitals,  

[7:4:66,290] ambulance companies, and medical supply vendors, to promote and improve disaster preparedness and emergency medical  

[7:5:66,300] response in California.  

[8:0:66,317] Emergency Medical Services Personnel Division  

[9:0:66,335] The Emergency Medical Services Personnel Division is responsible for licensing and enforcement actions of all active  

[9:1:66,345] paramedics throughout the state. The Division develops and implements regulations that set training, certification and licensure  

[9:2:66,356] standards, and the scope of practice for various emergency medical services personnel. The Division also sets standards for,  

[9:3:66,366] and approves, training programs in: pediatric first aid, CPR,   preventive health practices for child day care providers, and school  

[9:4:66,376] bus drivers. It also develops standards for emergency medical dispatcher training, pre-arrival emergency care instructions, and  

[9:5:66,386] the epinephrine auto-injector training program.  

[9:6:66,404] Emergency Medical Services Systems Division  

[10:0:66,422] The Emergency Medical Services Systems Division is responsible for developing and implementing emergency medical  

[10:1:66,432] services systems throughout California, including the support of local Health Information Exchange projects that will allow the  

[10:2:66,442] state to collect more meaningful data so that emergency medical services providers can deliver better patient care. The  

[10:3:66,452] Division also oversees system development and implementation by the local Emergency Medical Services agencies, the  

[10:4:66,462] statewide trauma system, and emergency medical dispatcher and communication standards.   Additionally, it   establishes  

[10:5:66,473] regulations and guidelines for local agencies; reviews and approves local plans to ensure they meet the minimum state  

[10:6:66,483] standards; coordinates injury and illness prevention activities with the California Department of Public Health and the Office of  

[10:7:66,493] Traffic Safety; manages the state's emergency medical services data and quality improvement process; conducts Ambulance  

[10:8:66,503] Exclusive Operating Area evaluations; oversees the operation of California's Poison Control System; and manages the  

[10:9:66,513] Emergency Medical Services for Children programs.

[5:0:66,282] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,302] 3835 - HEALTH CARE WORKFORCE  

[6:0:66,322] The Health Care Workforce Program, through the Health Care Workforce Development Division and the Health Professions  

[6:1:66,332] Education Foundation, improves access to medical, mental, and dental health care providers in underserved areas throughout  

[6:2:66,342] California. The Program conducts research to identify areas of unmet need and administers grants that provide financial  

[6:3:66,353] incentives to individuals and institutions to increase the number of providers in those areas. The Program promotes health care  

[6:4:66,363] workforce diversity and cultural competency. It includes the following programs:  

[6:5:65,380] • Song-Brown Health Care Workforce Training Program  

[7:0:65,397] • Mental Health Services Act Workforce Education and Training Program  

[7:1:65,413] • California State Loan Repayment Program  

[7:2:65,429] • Health Care Workforce Clearinghouse Program  

[7:3:65,445] • Health Professions Career Opportunity Training Program  

[7:4:65,461] • Health Workforce Pilot Projects Program  

[7:5:65,478] • Shortage Designation Program  

[8:0:65,494] • Health Professions Education Foundation Programs  

[8:1:66,512] 3840 - FACILITIES DEVELOPMENT  

[9:0:66,529] The Facilities Development Program safeguards public health, safety, and general welfare through regulation of the design and  

[9:1:66,539] construction of health care facilities, including compliance with seismic safety requirements, to ensure they are capable of  

[9:2:66,550] providing sustained services to the public.  

[9:3:66,567] 3845 - CAL-MORTGAGE LOAN INSURANCE  

[10:0:66,585] The Cal-Mortgage Program is modeled after federal home mortgage insurance programs and insures loans to public and  

[10:1:66,595] nonprofit health care facilities for construction, renovation, and expansion projects. The Program underwrites loans, monitors  

[10:2:66,605] the Cal-Mortgage insured loan portfolio, and administers the Health Facility Construction Loan Insurance Fund. By facilitating  

[10:3:66,616] access to private capital at no cost to taxpayers, the Program has improved the delivery of health care throughout California.  

[10:4:66,633] 3855 - HEALTH CARE INFORMATION AND QUALITY ANALYSIS 

[11:0:66,651] The Health Care Information Program sets standards for, collects, and maintains financial and utilization data from  

[11:1:66,661] approximately 6,000 licensed health facilities in California, as well as comprehensive demographic, diagnostic, and treatment  

[11:2:66,671] data for all patients discharged from licensed hospitals, treated in emergency departments, or having had an ambulatory  

[11:3:66,682] surgery procedure in hospital surgical clinics. This information is used by health care policymakers, health care providers,  

[11:4:66,692] health planners, public and private sector health care purchasers, researchers, consumers, and the media. To further this  

[11:5:66,702] mission, the Health Care Information Program is implementing new health care cost transparency data programs to collect and  

[12:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:1:66,93] disparities, and reduce health care costs.

[4:0:184,137] 4150   Department of Managed Health Care  

[4:1:66,158] The Department of Managed Health Care protects health care consumers   and ensures a stable health care delivery system in  

[4:2:66,168] California. The Department achieves this mission by:  

[4:3:65,186] • Licensing and regulating the full scope of managed care models, including all Health Maintenance Organizations (HMO) in  

[4:4:76,196] the state, Preferred Provider Organizations (PPO), Exclusive Provider Organizations (EPO), Point-of-Service (POS) products  

[4:5:76,206] and Medi-Cal managed care plans. The Department also licenses and conducts financial reviews of Medicare Advantage  

[4:6:76,216] and Part D plans and licenses and regulates specialized health plans including chiropractic, dental, vision, psychological  

[4:7:76,227] (behavioral health) and pharmacy.  

[4:8:65,243] • Enforcing the Knox-Keene Health Care Service Plan Act of 1975, as amended.  

[4:9:65,259] • Conducting medical surveys and financial examinations to verify that health plans are complying with the law and are  

[4:10:76,269] financially stable to serve their enrollees.  

[4:11:65,285] • Operating a 24-hour-a-day Help Center to resolve health care consumer complaints and administer the Independent Medical  

[4:12:76,296] Review program.  

[4:13:65,312] • Reviewing proposed health plan rate changes for sufficient justification and reasonableness.  

[4:14:65,328] • Monitoring the financial solvency of the medical groups with whom health plans contract to provide health benefits to their  

[4:15:76,338] enrollees.  

[5:0:65,354] • Convening the Financial Solvency Standards Board, comprised of people with expertise in the medical, financial and health  

[5:1:76,365] plan industries, to advise the Director on strategies to keep the managed care industry financially stable.

[6:0:66,367] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,387] 3870 - HEALTH PLAN PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,407] The Health Plan Program's primary objective is to regulate managed health care plans and assist consumers to resolve  

[7:1:66,417] disputes with health plans. The program's key functions to achieve this objective are to: license managed health care plans,  

[7:2:66,428] conduct routine and non-routine financial exams and medical surveys, review proposed premium rate increases, assist  

[7:3:66,438] consumers with health care issues and enable managed health care patients to receive the medical care and services to which  

[7:4:66,448] they are entitled, and operate a consumer services toll-free complaint line (1-888-466-2219).

[8:0:228,404] 4170   Department of Aging  

[9:0:66,426] The Department of Aging's mission is to promote the independence and well-being of older adults, adults with disabilities, and  

[9:1:66,436] families through:  

[9:2:65,454] • Access to information and services to improve the quality of their lives,  

[9:3:65,470] • Opportunities for community involvement,  

[9:4:65,486] • Support to family members providing care, and  

[9:5:65,502] • Collaboration with other state and local agencies.  

[9:6:66,520] As the federally designated State Unit on Aging, the Department administers federal Older Americans Act programs that  

[9:7:66,530] provide a wide variety of community-based supportive services and administers the Health Insurance Counseling and  

[9:8:66,540] Advocacy Program. The Department also administers two Medi-Cal programs: it contracts directly with agencies that operate  

[9:9:66,551] the Multipurpose Senior Services Program (MSSP) and provides oversight for the MSSP waiver, and certifies Community-

[9:10:66,561] Based Adult Services centers for participation in Medicaid.  

[10:0:66,581] The Department administers most of these programs through contracts with the state's 33 local Area Agencies on Aging. At the  

[10:1:66,591] local level, Area Agencies on Aging contract for and coordinate this array of community-based services to older adults, adults  

[10:2:66,602] with disabilities, family caregivers, and residents of long-term care facilities.

[6:0:66,321] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,340] 3890 - NUTRITION  

[7:0:66,360] The Nutrition Program provides nutritionally-balanced meals, nutrition education, and nutrition counseling to individuals 60  

[7:1:66,370] years of age or older. In addition to promoting better health through improved nutrition, the program focuses on reducing the  

[7:2:66,381] isolation of the elderly and providing a link to other social and supportive services such as transportation, information and  

[7:3:66,391] assistance, employment, and education.  

[7:4:66,409] 3895 - SENIOR COMMUNITY EMPLOYMENT SERVICE  

[8:0:66,429] The federal Senior Community Service Employment Program, Title V of the Older Americans Act, provides part-time subsidized  

[8:1:66,439] training and employment in community service agencies for low-income persons 55 years of age and older. The program also  

[8:2:66,449] promotes transition to unsubsidized employment.  

[8:3:66,467] 3900 - SUPPORTIVE SERVICES  

[9:0:66,485] This program provides supportive services in the community to adults 60 years of age or older, their family caregivers,  

[9:1:66,495] grandparents caring for grandchildren, and residents of long-term care facilities. Services include information and assistance,  

[9:2:66,505] legal assistance, transportation, respite in-home support, senior center activities, elder abuse prevention, and the Long-Term  

[9:3:66,515] Care Ombudsman. Older Americans Act Titles III and VII fund these services to enable individuals to access the support  

[9:4:66,526] necessary for them to remain independent in their communities, continue in their caregiving role, and/or receive long-term care  

[9:5:66,536] services appropriate to their needs.  

[10:0:66,553] 3905 - COMMUNITY-BASED PROGRAMS AND PROJECTS  

[11:0:66,571] This program includes the community-based Health Insurance Counseling and Advocacy Program (HICAP). HICAP provides  

[11:1:66,581] personalized counseling, community education, and outreach events for Medicare beneficiaries. HICAP is the primary local  

[11:2:66,592] source for accurate and objective information and assistance with Medicare benefits, prescription drug plans, and health plans.  

[11:3:66,609] 3910 - MEDI-CAL PROGRAMS  

[12:0:66,627] This program includes oversight of the Multipurpose Senior Services Program (MSSP) and Community-Based Adult Services  

[12:1:66,637] (CBAS) program. CBAS is a community-based day health program that provides services to adults 18 years of age or over who  

[12:2:66,647] are at risk of needing institutional care due to chronic medical, cognitive, or mental health conditions and/or disabilities. The  

[12:3:66,658] Department certifies CBAS centers for participation in the Medi-Cal Program. Under a 1915(c) Medicaid home and community-

[12:4:66,668] based services waiver, MSSP provides health and social care management to prevent premature and unnecessary long-term  

[12:5:66,678] care institutionalization of frail adults aged 65 or older who otherwise would be placed in a nursing facility.  

[13:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[5:0:66,269] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,289] 3930 - COMMISSION ON AGING  

[6:0:66,306] The Commission's statutory responsibilities include: assisting with the development of the Department of Aging's State Plan on  

[6:1:66,317] Aging, monitoring the plan's progress, and information-gathering. As part of its information-gathering responsibility, the  

[6:2:66,327] Commission holds meetings and public hearings around the state to address the issues and concerns of older Californians,  

[6:3:66,337] their families, and caregivers. The Commission uses the information gathered from these meetings and public hearings to  

[6:4:66,347] develop initiatives and projects focused on older Californians and their caregivers. The Commission also assisted with the  

[6:5:66,357] development and implementation of the state's Alzheimer's Disease Plan, holds membership on the Master Plan for Aging  

[6:6:66,368] Stakeholder Advisory Committee, and administers the Area Agency on Aging Advisory Councils of California. The Area Agency  

[6:7:66,378] on Aging Advisory Councils of California is supported solely by voluntary contributions made through a check-off box included  

[6:8:66,388] on the state income tax form.

[1:0:169,83] 4260   State Department of Health Care Services  

[2:0:66,105] The mission of the   State Department of Health Care Services (DHCS) is to provide Californians with access to affordable,  

[3:0:66,115] integrated, high-quality health care, including medical, dental, mental health, substance use treatment services, and long-term  

[3:1:66,125] care. To fulfill its mission, DHCS finances and administers a number of individual health care service delivery programs,  

[4:0:66,135] including the state's Medicaid Program (Medi-Cal), which provides health care services to low-income persons and families  

[4:1:66,146] who meet defined eligibility requirements.

[3:0:66,93] California Code of Regulations, Titles 9, 17 and 22.  

[4:0:66,130] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[5:0:65,149] • COVID-19 Estimate Impacts—The Budget includes costs of $8.1 billion total funds and savings of $155.1 million General  

[5:1:76,160] Fund for COVID-19 impacts on the Medi-Cal program. Costs are primarily attributable to a significant increase in caseload  

[5:2:76,170] associated with projected unemployment and the Medi-Cal response to COVID-19, offset by an assumed increase in the  

[5:3:76,180] Federal Medical Assistance Percentage (FMAP). Specifically, the Budget assumes that caseload will peak at 14.5 million in  

[5:4:76,190] July 2020, or about 2.0 million above what caseload would have been absent the COVID-19 pandemic. 

[6:0:65,206] • Suspensions—In addition to suspensions included in the 2019 Budget Act, the Budget   suspends all Proposition 56 programs  

[6:1:76,217] other than women’s health, family planning, and the Loan Repayment Program on July 1, 2021. The suspension will be lifted  

[6:2:76,227] if the Administration determines through the 2021 Budget Act process that there is sufficient General Fund revenue to  

[6:3:76,237] support all suspended programs in the subsequent two fiscal years. 

[7:0:65,253] • Nursing Facility Financing—The Budget includes $185.6 million ($92.8 million General Fund) in 2020-21 to extend through  

[7:1:76,263] December 1, 2022 the financing system for skilled nursing facilities, originally established pursuant to Chapter 875, Statutes  

[7:2:76,274] of 2004 (AB 1629). In addition, the Budget includes a 10-percent rate increase for SNFs assumed to be in effect for four  

[7:3:76,284] months during the COVID-19 emergency, at a General Fund cost of $72.4 million in 2019-20 and $41.6 million in 2020-21.  

[8:0:65,300] • 340B Supplemental Payment Pool—The Budget includes $52.5 million ($26.3 million General Fund) in 2020-21 to provide  

[8:1:76,310] supplemental payments to specified non-hospital clinics who participated in the federal 340B pharmacy program. These  

[8:2:76,320] payments grow to $105 million ($52.5 million General Fund) in 2021-22 and annually thereafter.  

[9:0:65,337] • Managed Care Efficiencies—The Budget implements changes to the way that managed care capitation rates are  

[9:1:76,347] determined. These changes include various acuity, efficiency, and cost containment adjustments. These adjustments would  

[9:2:76,357] be effective for the managed care rate year starting January 1, 2021, and would yield savings of $193.6 million ($63 million  

[9:3:76,367] General Fund) in 2020-21. Additionally, the Budget assumes a 1.5 percent rate reduction for the July 1, 2019, through  

[9:4:76,377] December 31, 2020, period, resulting in savings of $586 million ($182 million General Fund) in 2020-21. The Budget does  

[9:5:76,388] not implement a maximum fee schedule for inpatient services in the managed care program.  

[10:0:65,404] • Hearing Aids Grant Program—The Budget includes $352,000 General Fund in 2020-21 to administer and establish a  

[10:1:76,414] program to assist with the cost of hearing aids and related services for children without health insurance coverage in  

[10:2:76,424] households with incomes up to 600 percent of the federal poverty level, no sooner than July 1, 2021. The Budget assumes  

[10:3:76,434] ongoing costs of approximately $15 million General Fund to provide and administer this benefit. 

[11:0:65,451] • Managed Care Organization Tax—The Budget includes $1.7 billion in General Fund savings associated with the federal  

[11:1:76,461] government’s approval of a three-year managed care organization (MCO) provider tax. The MCO tax is estimated to result in  

[11:2:76,471] approximately $4.9 billion in General Fund savings over the full three years of the tax.

[7:0:66,564] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[7:1:66,583] 3960010 - MEDICAL CARE SERVICES (MEDI-CAL)  

[8:0:66,604] Medi-Cal is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of health care services to low-income Californians. Medi-Cal  

[8:1:66,614] provides access to quality medical care in a fiscally prudent manner through both fee-for-service and managed care delivery  

[8:2:66,624] systems. Medi-Cal activities are carried out through the following divisions: Integrated Systems of Care; Managed Care Quality  

[8:3:66,634] and Monitoring; Managed Care Operations; Medi-Cal Eligibility; Medi-Cal Dental Services; Pharmacy Benefits; Benefits; Safety  

[8:4:66,644] Net Financing; Capitated Rates Development; Fee-For-Service Rates Development; Local Governmental Financing; Behavioral  

[8:5:66,655] Health Community Services; Fiscal Forecasting; Medi-Cal Behavioral Health; Audits and Investigations; Program Operations  

[8:6:66,665] (California Medicaid Management Information Systems, Provider Enrollment, and Clinical Assurance); Research and Analytic  

[8:7:66,675] Studies; Third Party Liability and Recovery; and Information Management. Additional Program Offices include: the Office of  

[8:8:66,685] Family Planning.

[7:2:66,248] prostate cancer treatment services to low-income, under-insured, or uninsured men. These services are provided through  

[8:0:66,258] the   Behavioral Health Community   Services Division, Behavioral Health Licensing and Certification Division, the Every Woman

[6:0:207,213] 4265   Department of Public Health  

[7:0:66,234] The California Department of Public Health (Public Health) is dedicated to optimizing the health and well-being of all  

[7:1:66,245] Californians through the following core activities:  

[7:2:65,262] • Protecting the public from communicable diseases.  

[8:0:65,279] • Protecting the public from unhealthy and unsafe environments, and improving social determinants of health and healthy  

[8:1:76,289] communities.  

[9:0:65,305] • Preventing disease, disability, and premature death; and reducing or eliminating health disparities by embedding health and  

[9:1:76,315] mental health equity language, tools, and approaches into all public health and partner agency policies, programs, systems,  

[9:2:76,325] and resource allocation.  

[9:3:65,342] • Preparing for and responding to public health emergencies.  

[10:0:65,358] • Producing and disseminating data to evaluate population health status; inform people, institutions and communities; and to  

[10:1:76,368] guide public health strategies, programs, and actions.  

[10:2:65,384] • Promoting healthy lifestyles for individuals and families in their communities and workplaces.  

[10:3:65,400] • Providing access to quality, population-based health services.  

[11:0:66,418] Because Public Health's programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has a capital outlay program to  

[11:1:66,428] support this need. For the specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[9:0:66,531] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[10:0:65,550] • COVID-19 Testing and Resources—The Budget includes $5.9 million General Fund, $4.8 million of which is ongoing, to  

[10:1:76,560] support laboratory staff to increase the state laboratories’ testing capacity, and to purchase equipment and laboratory  

[10:2:76,570] supplies that are specifically utilized for COVID-19 testing. Additionally, resources will support emergency coordination,  

[10:3:76,581] communication, and response, and provide ongoing support for public health laboratory capacity and disease surveillance.  

[11:0:65,597] • Licensing and Certification—The Budget includes $3.1 million State Licensing and Certification Program Fund and 75  

[12:0:76,607] positions to support surveying, application processing, and technical support functions. The Budget also includes $21 million  

[12:1:76,617] State Licensing and Certification Program Fund to implement year two of the Los Angeles County Contract.  

[13:0:65,633] • Ongoing Infectious Disease Prevention—The Budget makes ongoing $5 million General Fund each for STD, human  

[13:1:76,644] immunodeficiency virus (HIV), and hepatitis C virus prevention and control that otherwise would have been suspended on  

[13:2:76,654] January 1, 2022.  

[14:0:65,670] • Cannabis Surveillance and Education—The Budget includes $20.8 million in 2020-21 and to support 87 existing permanent  

[14:1:76,680] positions and mandated activities of the Medicinal and Adult-Use Cannabis Regulations and Safety Act and to continue the  

[14:2:76,690] Medical Marijuana Identification Card Program (MMICP).

[5:0:66,219] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,239] 4040010 - Emergency Preparedness  

[6:0:66,256] The Public Health Emergency Preparedness program coordinates preparedness and response activities for all public health  

[6:1:66,266] emergencies, including natural disasters, acts of terrorism, and pandemic diseases. The program plans and supports surge  

[6:2:66,277] capacity in the medical care and public health systems to meet needs during emergencies. The program also administers  

[6:3:66,287] federal and state funds that support Public Health emergency preparedness activities.  

[6:4:66,305] 4045 - PUBLIC AND ENVIRONMENTAL HEALTH  

[7:0:66,322] The Public and Environmental Health programs provide public health services of: communicable disease control; chronic  

[7:1:66,332] disease and injury prevention; environmental public health; maternal, child, and family health; and vital records. These  

[7:2:66,343] programs function as part of the greater public health system throughout California.  

[7:3:66,360] 4045010 - Healthy Communities  

[8:0:66,378] This program works to support healthy communities and   address health inequities by directing initiatives focused on chronic  

[8:1:66,388] disease prevention and management, environmental health, occupational health, injury and violence prevention, and substance  

[8:2:66,398] use and addiction. This program includes the Office of Oral Health, Office of Problem Gambling, California Tobacco Control  

[8:3:66,409] Branch, Childhood Lead Poisoning Prevention Branch, Chronic Disease Control Branch, Chronic Disease Surveillance and  

[8:4:66,419] Research Branch, Environmental Health Laboratory Branch, Environmental Health Investigations Branch, Nutrition Education  

[8:5:66,429] and Obesity Prevention Branch, Occupational Health Branch, and Injury and Violence Prevention Branch.  

[8:6:66,447] 4045023 - Infectious Diseases  

[9:0:66,464] This program works to prevent and control infectious diseases such as: HIV/AIDS, viral hepatitis, influenza and other vaccine-

[9:1:66,475] preventable illnesses, sexually transmitted diseases, tuberculosis, emerging infections, and foodborne illnesses. This program  

[9:2:66,485] includes Communicable Disease Control, the Office of AIDS, the Office of Binational Border Health, and the Office of Refugee  

[9:3:66,495] Health.  

[9:4:66,513] 4045032 - Family Health  

[10:0:66,530] This program works to improve and reduce disparities in health outcomes for girls and women of reproductive age, pregnant  

[10:1:66,541] and postpartum women, infants, children, adolescents, and their families. This program includes Genetic Disease Screening;  

[10:2:66,551] Maternal, Child, and Adolescent Health; and the Special Supplemental Nutrition Program for Women, Infants, and Children.  

[10:3:66,569] 4045041 - Health Statistics and Informatics  

[11:0:66,586] This program develops data systems and facilitates the collection, validation, analysis, and dissemination of health information.  

[11:1:66,596] This program includes Vital Records, Public Health Policy and Research, and Public Health Informatics.

[9:0:66,456] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[10:0:66,475] The Department of Public Health operates a single laboratory facility in Richmond, California. The laboratory provides  

[10:1:66,485] analytical, diagnostic, developmental, evaluative, epidemiological, reference, quality control, educational, training, and  

[10:2:66,496] consultative laboratory services related to the protection and promotion of public health. The Richmond campus consists of  

[10:3:66,506] 697,000 gross square feet of laboratory, office, and support facilities on 29 acres.

[6:0:176,213] 4300   Department of Developmental Services  

[7:0:66,235] The Department of Developmental Services is responsible under the Lanterman Developmental Disabilities Services Act for  

[7:1:66,245] providing persons with developmental disabilities the services and supports they need to lead more independent and  

[7:2:66,255] productive lives and to make choices and decisions about their lives. The Department sets broad policy and provides  

[7:3:66,265] leadership for developmental services statewide; establishes priorities, standards, and procedures within which the  

[7:4:66,276] developmental services program operates; monitors, reviews, and evaluates service delivery; and helps to remediate problems  

[7:5:66,286] that arise. Services are delivered through a statewide network of 21 private, nonprofit, locally based community agencies  

[7:6:66,296] known as regional centers as well as through a developmental center and a state-operated community facility. The Department,  

[7:7:66,306] through the 21 regional centers, oversees coordination of services to persons with developmental disabilities; provides that  

[7:8:66,316] such services are planned, provided, and meet the needs and choices of these individuals at each stage of their lives; and, to  

[7:9:66,327] the extent possible, accomplishes these goals in the individual's home community.  

[8:0:66,344] Because the Department of Developmental Services' programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has  

[8:1:66,355] a capital outlay program to support this need. For the specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure  

[8:2:66,365] Overview."

[9:0:66,242] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[10:0:65,262] • Supplemental Rate Increases for Additional Service Codes—The Budget includes $18 million ($10.8 million General Fund) in  

[10:1:76,272] 2020-21 and 2021-22 to provide supplemental rate increases for Early Start Specialized Therapeutic Services, Infant  

[10:2:76,282] Development and Independent Living Services. This approach is consistent with the supplemental rate increases included in  

[10:3:76,292] the 2019 Budget Act. The increased funding for the three services will be suspended on December 31, 2021. The  

[10:4:76,302] suspension will be lifted if the Administration determines through the 2021 Budget Act process that there is sufficient General  

[10:5:76,313] Fund revenue to support all suspended programs.  

[11:0:65,329] • Uniform Holiday Schedule—The Budget includes $51.5 million ($31.3 million General Fund) in 2020-21 to suspend  

[11:1:76,339] implementation of the Uniform Holiday Schedule. The funding will be suspended on December 31, 2021. The suspension will  

[11:2:76,349] be lifted if the Administration determines through the 2021 Budget Act process that there is sufficient General Fund revenue  

[11:3:76,359] to support all suspended programs.  

[12:0:65,376] • COVID-19 Impacts—The Budget includes $336.7 million ($237.5 million General Fund) in 2020-21 to reflect impacts of  

[12:1:76,386] COVID-19 on the developmental services system. These changes reflect increased costs associated with increased  

[12:2:76,396] utilization in purchase of services specific to residential settings, respite, and personal attendants. These costs also reflect  

[12:3:76,406] surge development at the developmental centers and in the community.  

[13:0:65,422] • Incompetent to Stand Trial (IST) Capacity—The Budget includes $16.4 million General Fund in 2020-21 to activate a 20-bed  

[13:1:76,433] unit at Porterville Developmental Center (PDC) and develop five enhanced behavioral support homes to increase capacity  

[13:2:76,443] for IST placements and secure community resources for individuals at PDC. The increased funding for the 20-bed unit PDC  

[13:3:76,453] will sunset on June 30, 2023.  

[14:0:65,469] • Fairview Developmental Center Warm-Shutdown—The Budget includes $11.9 million General Fund to extend the warm-

[14:1:76,479] shutdown period at Fairview Developmental Center through 2020-21 until a site assessment is completed to inform the  

[14:2:76,490] disposition of the property.

[5:0:66,552] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,571] 4140 - COMMUNITY SERVICES PROGRAM  

[6:0:66,591] Through the network of regional centers, the Department supports the development and maintenance of services for eligible  

[6:1:66,601] persons with developmental disabilities who reside in the community. The regional centers directly provide or coordinate the  

[6:2:66,612] following services and supports: (1) information and referral, (2) assessment and diagnosis, (3) counseling, (4) lifelong  

[6:3:66,622] individualized planning and service coordination, (5) purchase of necessary services included in the individual program plan,  

[6:4:66,632] (6) assistance in finding and using community and other resources, (7) advocacy for the protection of legal, civil, and service  

[6:5:66,642] rights, (8) early intervention services for infants and their families, (9) family support, (10) planning, placement, and monitoring  

[6:6:66,652] for 24-hour out-of-home care, (11) training and educational opportunities for individuals and families, (12) community education  

[6:7:66,663] about developmental disabilities, and (13) habilitation services.  

[7:0:66,680] 4145 - STATE-OPERATED RESIDENTIAL AND COMMUNITY FACILITIES PROGRAM  

[8:0:66,698] The Department currently operates two residential facilities: Fairview Developmental Center (Orange County) and Porterville  

[8:1:66,708] Developmental Center (Tulare County). Secure treatment services are provided at the Porterville Developmental Center  

[9:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

# === PAGE 130 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] 2020-21 STATE BUDGET — HHS   128 

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:141,29] 4300   Department of Developmental Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,83] for   individuals who have been found incompetent to stand trial due to their developmental disability. The Department is  

[3:1:66,93] projected to operate seven Stabilization, Training, Assistance, and Reintegration (STAR) residences by the   fall of 2020 in  

[3:2:66,103] Northern, Central, and Southern California   to provide acute crisis services in the community.   The Department also leases one  

[3:3:66,113] small community facility for persons who require specialized behavioral interventions: Canyon Springs, a 63-bed facility in  

[3:4:66,124] Cathedral City (Riverside County).  

[4:0:66,141] All   residential facilities are licensed as General Acute Care Hospitals with distinct parts for skilled nursing care and intermediate  

[4:1:66,152] care. Canyon Springs operates as an intermediate care facility, and STAR residences operate as community crisis homes.  

[4:2:66,162] Services at all facilities involve the provision of active treatment through residential and day programs on a 24-hour basis,  

[4:3:66,172] including appropriate medical and dental care, health maintenance activities, and assistance with activities of daily living,  

[4:4:66,182] training, education, and employment.  

[5:0:66,200] Individuals served in the STAR crisis   residences are committed by a court order to the Department for suitable treatment and  

[5:1:66,210] habilitation services during a crisis, and are provided services and supports necessary to prepare them for return to their  

[5:2:66,220] residential home or to transition to a new living option. The primary objective of this program   is to provide a safety net of  

[5:3:66,230] services that include providing care, treatment, crisis services, and habilitation services to residents based upon assessed  

[5:4:66,241] need and as outlined in each person's Individual Program Plan. These services are offered in the most efficient, effective, and  

[5:5:66,251] least restrictive manner to all individuals referred by the regional centers and/or the judicial system; and are designed to teach  

[5:6:66,261] individuals the skills for increased independence, provide for preservation or improvement of health and welfare, and enhance  

[5:7:66,271] personal competence in all areas of daily living.  

[6:0:66,289] Fairview Developmental Center and the non-secure treatment portion of Porterville Developmental Center transitioned the last  

[6:1:66,299] resident into a community setting in December 2019.  

[6:2:66,317] 4149 - PROGRAM ADMINISTRATION  

[7:0:66,337] The objective of this program is to: (1) provide overall management, planning and policy development, legal, legislative, audit,  

[7:1:66,347] and administrative services; (2) manage revenue and reimbursement collections from federal and state programs, insurance  

[7:2:66,358] companies, and private payers for the cost of services; (3) monitor regional center operations for compliance with statute,  

[7:3:66,368] regulations, and their contract with the Department; (4) provide central administrative and clinical management services to  

[7:4:66,378] the   two residential facilities and the leased small community facility to oversee the quality of services provided, compliance with  

[7:5:66,388] state licensing and federal certification requirements, protection of consumers and staff, and maintenance of facility structures  

[7:6:66,398] and grounds; and (5) oversee areas that include the development of policy and procedures for developmental center  

[8:0:66,409] operations, law enforcement and protective services, facility population management, program and fiscal oversight, and facility  

[8:1:66,419] planning and support.

[3:0:66,83] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[4:0:66,102] The Department of Developmental Services is responsible for the operation and maintenance of the facilities under its control,  

[4:1:66,113] including two state-owned and operated 24-hour care facilities and related buildings, grounds, and infrastructure. The facilities  

[4:2:66,123] are Fairview Developmental Center in Orange County and Porterville Developmental Center in Tulare County.  

[4:3:66,140] The developmental centers are comprised of approximately 2.3 million gross square feet in 319   buildings on 784 acres.   As of  

[4:4:66,151] December 2019, the Fairview Developmental Center and the Porterville General Treatment Area transitioned all former  

[4:5:66,161] residents to community living.   The Department will continue to maintain the Fairview property in warm shutdown mode until  

[4:6:66,171] disposition of the property.   The Department also operates two residences and is developing five more for Stabilization,  

[4:7:66,181] Training, Assistance, and Reintegration programs that provide acute crisis services in the community.   Additionally, the  

[4:8:66,191] Department is responsible for the maintenance of interior finishes and equipment at a 57,000 square foot leased facility in  

[4:9:66,202] Riverside County.   These facilities are used to aid the Department's mission   in providing medical, dental, and nursing care;  

[4:10:66,212] active treatment; supervision; education; and vocational training for residents with developmental disabilities.

[13:3:66,714] treatment for its patients in five state hospitals located in Atascadero, Coalinga, Metropolitan-Los Angeles, Napa, and

[5:0:66,181] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,201] 4380 - IN-PATIENT SERVICES PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,218] The In-Patient Services Program administers the California state hospital system, the Conditional Release Program, the Sex  

[7:1:66,229] Offender Commitment Program, the Restoration of Competency Program, and the treatment and evaluation of judicially and  

[7:2:66,239] civilly committed patients.  

[8:0:66,257] 4400 - ADMINISTRATION  

[9:0:66,274] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters oversees the California state hospital system, which provides mental health  

[9:1:66,284] services to patients admitted into Department of State Hospitals facilities. Program Administration includes headquarters  

[9:2:66,295] functions such as: policy development and management, licensing oversight, patients' rights coordination, clinical oversight,  

[9:3:66,305] data research, fiscal, personnel and contracts management, as well as legal services.  

[10:0:66,323] Hospital Administration includes centralized functions and services that directly affect patient care but are administered  

[10:1:66,333] centrally from headquarters.  

[11:0:66,350] 4400010 - HEADQUARTERS ADMINISTRATION  

[12:0:66,368] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters oversees the California state hospital system, which provides mental health  

[12:1:66,378] services to patients admitted into   its facilities. Headquarters Administration includes headquarters functions such as: policy  

[12:2:66,389] development and management, licensing oversight, patients' rights coordination, clinical oversight, data research, fiscal,  

[12:3:66,399] personnel and contracts management, as well as legal services.  

[13:0:66,416] 4400020 - HOSPITAL ADMINISTRATION  

[14:0:66,434] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters includes a Hospital Administration component. Hospital Administration includes  

[14:1:66,444] centralized functions and services that directly affect patient care but are administered centrally from headquarters such as:  

[14:2:66,455] technology services, hospital police and fire oversight, patient referral management, clinical recruitment, patient benefit and  

[14:3:66,465] billing management, and Medicare revenue collection.  

[15:0:66,482] 4410 - STATE HOSPITALS  

[16:0:66,500] The state hospital system includes five state hospitals located at Atascadero, Metropolitan-Los Angeles, Napa, Patton, and  

[16:1:66,510] Coalinga. Mental health treatment services at all facilities are delivered by clinical teams who provide full-time inpatient care to  

[16:2:66,521] those with mental illness and those incapable of living in the community. The state hospitals treat the following types of  

[16:3:66,531] patients: civil commitments under the Lanterman-Petris-Short Act (LPS); forensic commitments such as incompetent to stand  

[16:4:66,541] trial (IST), not guilty by reason of insanity (NGI), sexually violent predators (SVP), and mentally disordered offenders (MDO);  

[16:5:66,551] and prisoners with mental illness ( Coleman ) from CDCR.  

[17:0:66,569] 4410010 - ATASCADERO  

[18:0:66,587] The Department of State Hospitals-Atascadero opened in 1954 and is located on the Central Coast of California in Atascadero  

[18:1:66,597] (San Luis Obispo County). The hospital is a self-contained psychiatric hospital constructed within a security perimeter. The  

[18:2:66,607] majority of the all-male patient population is remanded for treatment by   Superior Courts or by CDCR pursuant to various  

[18:3:66,617] sections of the California Penal Code   and the Welfare and Institutions Code.  

[19:0:66,635] DSH-Atascadero primarily serves the following four patient types: MDO,  Coleman   patients from CDCR, IST, and   NGI.  

[20:0:66,653] 4410020 - COALINGA  

[21:0:66,670] The Department of State Hospitals-Coalinga opened in 2005 and is located on the western edge of Fresno County. The  

[21:1:66,680] hospital is California’s newest forensic mental health hospital and was created to primarily treat SVPs. It is a self-contained  

[21:2:66,691] psychiatric hospital constructed with a security perimeter. CDCR provides perimeter security as well as transportation of  

[21:3:66,701] patients to outside medical services and court proceedings. The majority of the all-male patient population is remanded for  

[22:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,83] treatment by   Superior Courts or CDCR pursuant to various sections of the California Penal Code and the Welfare and  

[3:1:66,93] Institutions Code.  

[4:0:66,111] DSH-Coalinga primarily serves MDOs,  Coleman   patients from CDCR,   and SVPs.  

[5:0:66,128] 4410030 - METROPOLITAN  

[6:0:66,146] The Department of State Hospitals-Metropolitan opened in 1916 and is located in Norwalk (Los Angeles County). The hospital  

[6:1:66,156] is an open style campus within a security perimeter. Due to concerns raised by the community, DSH-Metropolitan maintains a  

[6:2:66,167] formal agreement with the City of Norwalk and the Los Angeles County Sheriff not to accept patients charged with murder or a  

[6:3:66,177] sex crime, or that are at high risk for escape.  

[7:0:66,194] DSH-Metropolitan primarily serves the following four patient types: LPS, IST, MDO, and NGI.  

[8:0:66,212] 4410040 - NAPA  

[9:0:66,230] The Department of State Hospitals-Napa opened in 1875 and is located in Napa County. The hospital   was the first of the  

[9:1:66,240] five   State Hospitals, and is   the oldest California state hospital still in operation.   It has an open style campus with a security  

[9:2:66,250] perimeter.  

[10:0:66,268] DSH-Napa primarily serves the following four patient types: LPS, IST, MDO, and NGI.  

[11:0:66,286] 4410050 - PATTON  

[12:0:66,303] The Department of State Hospitals-Patton opened in 1893 and is located in San Bernardino County. The hospital has an open  

[12:1:66,314] style campus with a security perimeter. CDCR correctional officers provide perimeter security and transportation at DSH-Patton  

[12:2:66,324] as well as transportation of patients to outside medical services and some court proceedings.  

[13:0:66,341] DSH-Patton primarily serves the following four patient types: LPS, IST, MDO, and NGI.  

[14:0:66,359] 4410060 - HOSPITAL POLICE OFFICER ACADEMY  

[15:0:66,377] The Department of State Hospitals Police Officer (HPO) Academy is overseen by the Office of Protective Services, which is a  

[15:1:66,387] full service law enforcement agency that protects the safety and security of the state hospital facilities, staff and patients. DSH  

[15:2:66,397] provides training standards, model programs, cultural competency, program development, and a comprehensive training plan  

[15:3:66,407] to all protective services staff. The HPO Academy requires that cadets successfully complete 548 hours of multidisciplinary  

[15:4:66,418] training specific to the DSH police officer job specifications.  

[16:0:66,435] 4420 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE PROGRAM  

[17:0:66,456] The Conditional Release Program is the statewide system of community-based services for specified forensic patients.  

[17:1:66,466] Mandated as a state responsibility by the Governor's Mental Health Initiative of 1984, the program began operations on  

[17:2:66,476] January 1, 1986.  

[18:0:66,494] 4420010 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE PROGRAM  

[19:0:66,512] The Conditional Release Program General/Non-Sexually Violent Predators is comprised of Not Guilty by Reason of Insanity,  

[19:1:66,522] Mentally Disordered Offender, felony Incompetent to Stand Trial, and Mentally Disordered Sex Offender patients. Individuals  

[19:2:66,532] suitable for this program may be recommended by the state hospital medical director to the courts for outpatient treatment.  

[19:3:66,542] Currently, DSH contracts with seven county-operated and three private organizations   serving all 58 counties in the state with  

[19:4:66,552] non-SVP commitments.  

[20:0:66,570] 4420020 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE PROGRAM -   SEXUALLY VIOLENT PREDATORS  

[21:0:66,588] The Conditional Release Program-Sexually Violent Predators was added to the Conditional Release Program effective January  

[21:1:66,598] 1, 1996 per Welfare and Institutions Code 6604. Prior to the conditional release of the first sexual violent predator in  

[21:2:66,608] 2003,   conditional release providers did not have treatment services that would allow them to accept sexually violent predators  

[21:3:66,618] as patients, requiring the Department of State Hospitals to enter into an annual contract with a single private provider serving  

[21:4:66,629] 58 counties. Current statue requires the sexually violent predators be conditionally released to their county of domicile and  

[21:5:66,639] sufficient funding be available to provide treatment and supervision services when a sexually violent predator is conditionally  

[21:6:66,649] released into the community by court order.  

[22:0:66,667] 4430 - CONTRACTED PATIENT SERVICES  

[23:0:66,687] The Department of State Hospitals contracts with local entities to provide mental health services to some of its patients outside  

[23:1:66,697] of state hospital facilities. This includes both the   Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization Center in the Kern County as well as  

[23:2:66,707] various other   jail-based competency treatment programs.  

[24:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,83] 4430010 - ADMISSION, EVALUATION, STABILIZATION CENTER 

[4:0:66,101] The Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization Center in the Kern County Jail receives incompetent to stand trial patients  

[4:1:66,111] committed to the Department of State Hospitals directly from catchment counties in southern California. Patients receive a full  

[4:2:66,121] evaluation upon admission to determine whether they can be treated through the Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization  

[4:3:66,131] Center on a short-term basis or may need longer-term state hospital treatment. Patients considered to be short-term can be  

[4:4:66,141] treated and discharged directly from the Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization Center.  

[4:5:66,159] 4430020 - JAIL-BASED COMPETENCY TREATMENT  

[5:0:66,177] The Jail-Based Competency Treatment Program focuses on defendants deemed incompetent to stand trial and provides  

[5:1:66,187] mental health treatment to defendants in county jails, restoring them to competency, and allowing for participation in court  

[5:2:66,197] proceedings.  

[6:0:66,215] 4440 - EVALUATION AND FORENSIC SERVICES  

[7:0:66,233] Evaluation and Forensic Services is comprised of the Mentally Disordered Offender and the Sex Offender Commitment  

[7:1:66,243] Programs. Penal Code Sections 2960-2981 require that a prisoner who meets specific criteria be ordered by the Board of  

[7:2:66,253] Parole Hearings to be treated by State Hospitals as a condition of parole. The Department of State Hospitals performs  

[7:3:66,263] evaluations to determine if individuals may meet the statutory criteria for the Mentally Disordered Offender program. These  

[7:4:66,273] evaluations are used by the Board of Parole Hearings in determining whether a prisoner is committed to the Department of  

[7:5:66,284] State Hospitals as a condition of parole. Welfare and Institutions Code Section 6600 et seq. (Chapter 793, Statutes of 1995)  

[7:6:66,294] was enacted January 1, 1996, establishing a new category of civil commitment for persons found, upon release from prison, to  

[7:7:66,304] be sexually violent predators. The Sex Offender Commitment Program administers clinical screenings and performs  

[7:8:66,314] evaluations to determine if prisoners may meet the statutory criteria for a sexually violent predator commitment to the  

[7:9:66,324] Department of State Hospitals upon completion of their prison term. Superior Courts make the ultimate determination whether  

[7:10:66,335] an individual is likely to be a sexually violent predator and warrants forensic psychological evaluations by the Department of  

[7:11:66,345] State Hospitals.

[13:1:66,695] (MHSA), Adult and Older Adult System of Care Act and Children's Mental Health Services Act. The Commission's primary roles  

[13:2:66,706] include: (1) providing oversight, review, accountability, and evaluation of projects and programs supported by MHSA funds, (2)  

[13:3:66,716] assessing whether services that are provided pursuant to the MHSA are cost-effective and in accordance with recommended

[2:0:99,29] 4700   Department of Community Services and Development - Continued 

[3:0:66,83] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:1:66,102] 4181 - ENERGY PROGRAMS  

[4:0:66,123] The Energy Programs assist low-income households in meeting their immediate and long-term home energy needs through  

[4:1:66,133] financial assistance, energy conservation, weatherization and renewable energy services.  

[5:0:66,153] The Low-Income Home Energy Assistance Program (LIHEAP) provides financial assistance to eligible low-income households  

[5:1:66,164] to offset the costs of heating and/or cooling residential dwellings, assistance for weather-related or energy-related  

[5:2:66,174] emergencies, and weatherization services to improve the energy efficiency of low-income residential dwellings and safeguard  

[5:3:66,184] the health and safety of household occupants. This program may include a leveraging incentive program in which  

[5:4:66,194] supplementary LIHEAP funds can be obtained by LIHEAP grantees if non-federal leveraged home energy resources are used  

[5:5:66,204] along with LIHEAP weatherization related services.  

[6:0:66,225] The Department of Energy Weatherization Assistance Program provides weatherization to improve the energy efficiency of low-

[6:1:66,235] income residential dwellings and safeguard the health and safety of household occupants.  

[7:0:66,253] The Low-Income Weatherization Program (LIWP) provides weatherization and renewable energy services in low-income  

[7:1:66,263] single-family and multi-family dwellings within disadvantaged communities to help reduce greenhouse gas emissions. LIWP  

[7:2:66,273] includes projects such as weatherization and solar water heater and solar photovoltaic systems installations.  

[7:3:66,291] 4185 - COMMUNITY SERVICES  

[8:0:66,311] The Community Services Block Grant is designed to enable local government and private nonprofit community organizations to  

[8:1:66,321] help low-income families achieve and maintain self-sufficiency through a broad range of activities. These activities include  

[8:2:66,332] education, employment services, emergency services, housing, income support and management, and health and nutritional  

[8:3:66,342] services. Additionally, Community Services Block Grant funds are used by local community organizations to revitalize low-

[8:4:66,352] income communities.  

[9:0:66,370] The California Earned Income Tax Credit (Cal EITC) benefits low-income, working Californians by providing cash-back tax  

[9:1:66,380] credits to boost the income of eligible families.   Since 2017-18   CSD has worked with the Franchise Tax Board and non-profit  

[9:2:66,390] and community-based organizations to increase awareness of the Cal EITC and provide free tax preparation assistance to  

[9:3:66,400] Californians.  

[10:0:66,440] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM  

[11:0:352,463] 2018-19* 2019-20* 2020-21*

[0:0:66,13] 2020-21 STATE BUDGET — HHS   160 

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:170,29] 5160   Department of Rehabilitation - Continued 

[3:0:66,53] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:0:66,72] 4210 - VOCATIONAL REHABILITATION SERVICES  

[5:0:66,90] The Vocational Rehabilitation Services Program delivers vocational rehabilitation services to persons with disabilities through  

[5:1:66,100] vocational rehabilitation professionals in district and branch offices located throughout the state so that persons with disabilities  

[5:2:66,110] may prepare for and engage in competitive integrated employment and achieve economic self-sufficiency. In addition, the  

[5:3:66,121] Department has cooperative agreements with state and local agencies (secondary and postsecondary education, mental  

[5:4:66,131] health, and welfare) to provide services to consumers. The Department operates under a federal Order of Selection process,  

[5:5:66,141] which gives priority to persons with the most significant disabilities.  

[6:0:66,159] Persons with disabilities who are eligible for the Department's vocational rehabilitation services may be provided a full range of  

[6:1:66,169] services, including vocational assessment, assistive technology, vocational and educational training, job placement, supported  

[6:2:66,179] employment and independent living skills training to maximize their ability to live and work independently within their  

[6:3:66,189] communities. The Department provides career counseling and information and referral services to encourage individuals  

[6:4:66,200] working in non-competitive, non-integrated settings to work toward and achieve competitive integrated employment.  

[7:0:66,217] The Department additionally provides pre-employment transition student services, known as DOR Student Services, and  

[7:1:66,227] auxiliary aids and services necessary to participate in such services to a wide range of students with disabilities, ages 16  

[7:2:66,238] through 21 (or upon matriculation from high school, whichever is later), including many who may benefit from early career  

[7:3:66,248] development. DOR Student Services include job exploration counseling, work-based learning experiences, postsecondary  

[7:4:66,258] education counseling, workplace readiness training, and instruction in self-advocacy. 

[8:0:66,276] The Department provides comprehensive training and technical assistance to enable persons who are blind or visually  

[8:1:66,286] impaired to support themselves in the operation of vending stands, snack bars, and cafeterias. Prevocational, including  

[8:2:66,296] employment readiness, services are provided by the Orientation Center for the Blind to consumers with vision loss to prepare  

[8:3:66,306] them for vocational rehabilitation services and independent living.  

[9:0:66,324] The Department works with public and private organizations to develop and improve community-based vocational rehabilitation  

[9:1:66,334] services for the Department's consumers. The Department sets standards, certifies Community Rehabilitation Programs, and  

[9:2:66,344] establishes fees for services provided to its consumers.  

[10:0:66,362] The Department works with the federal government to administer the California Career Innovations Demonstration Project to  

[10:1:66,372] identify how to increase the self-sufficiency of students with disabilities by providing work-based learning experiences and  

[10:2:66,383] planned education to prepare them for workplace success.  

[11:0:66,400] 4215 - INDEPENDENT LIVING SERVICES  

[12:0:66,418] The Department funds, administers, and supports 28 non-profit independent living centers in communities located throughout  

[12:1:66,428] California. Each independent living center provides services necessary to assist consumers to live independently   with full  

[12:2:66,438] inclusion   in their communities. Core services consist of information and referral, peer counseling, individual and systems  

[12:3:66,449] change advocacy, independent living skills, housing assistance, personal assistance referral services, transition and diversion  

[12:4:66,459] services to community based living, and   transition services to postsecondary life for youth.  

[13:0:66,476] The Department administers and supports the Traumatic Brain Injury (TBI) Program. In coordination with consumers and their  

[13:1:66,487] families, seven service providers throughout California provide a coordinated post-acute care service model for persons with  

[13:2:66,497] TBI, including supported living, community reintegration, vocational supportive services, public awareness, and support for  

[13:3:66,507] family, friends, and professionals within the TBI community. The Department also works with the federal government to  

[13:4:66,517] administer a TBI partnership grant with which a state TBI Advisory Board has been established for the purpose of creating a  

[13:5:66,527] statewide TBI registry, needs assessment, and resource plan.  

[14:0:66,545] The Department administers the federal Older Individuals Who Are Blind program that supports 17 non-profit community-based  

[14:1:66,555] organizations throughout California that provide blindness-related independent living services necessary to assist visually  

[14:2:66,566] impaired consumers age 55 or older to live independently and be productive in their communities. Core services consist of low  

[14:3:66,576] vision training, assistive technology devices and training, orientation and mobility, communication skills, independent living  

[14:4:66,586] skills development, self-advocacy, adjustment counseling, transportation, and supportive services.  

[15:0:66,604] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION  

[16:0:66,621] The Administration Program provides overall management planning, policy development, and administrative support services  

[16:1:66,632] to departmental programs.  

[17:0:66,672] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM

[9:0:66,446] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[9:1:66,465] 4250 - STATE COUNCIL SERVICES  

[10:0:66,486] The State Independent Living Council, in conjunction with the Department of Rehabilitation, is responsible for developing a  

[10:1:66,496] state plan for independent living and for monitoring, reviewing and evaluating the implementation of that plan. The Council also  

[10:2:66,506] interacts with similar statewide councils to enhance the effectiveness of the network of centers that provide independent living  

[10:3:66,516] services in California. The Council is required by the Federal Rehabilitation Act of 1973, as amended, in order for the state to  

[10:4:66,526] receive financial assistance for Independent Living Services and the Centers for Independent Living. The Council serves as an  

[10:5:66,537] educational resource on disability and independent living for the Governor, other state agencies, the Legislature, the general  

[10:6:66,547] public, and a variety of statewide and national organizations.

[8:0:66,346] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[9:0:66,365] Disregard Payments to Families—The Budget increases the amount of child support payments passed through to CalWORKS  

[9:1:66,375] families, effective January 1, 2022, from the current $50 to $100 for a family with one child and $200 for a family with two or  

[9:2:66,385] more children. This change is anticipated to result in an additional $34 million annually passed-through to approximately  

[9:3:66,395] 160,000 CalWORKs families. The Budget includes $800,000 ($300,000 General Fund) in 2020-21 for the necessary  

[9:4:66,406] automation changes needed to implement the proposal in 2021-22.  

[10:0:66,423] The Budget includes   an ongoing   $46.4 million   General Fund reduction   for child support administration, that will be  

[10:1:66,434] restored,   should federal funds   become available by October 15,   2020. This reduction includes:  

[10:2:65,451] • Savings of $38.1 million to revert Local Child Support Agency Funding to 2018 levels.  

[10:3:65,467] • Savings of $8.3 million to reduce state operations and contracts cost.

[6:1:66,304] parental responsibilities by establishing paternity for children, establishing court orders for financial and medical support, and  

[6:2:66,314] enforcing those orders. The program operates as the single state entity designed to administer the federally mandated Title IV-

[6:3:66,325] D child support program in California. Operation of this program is required for the state to continue to receive the Temporary  

[6:4:66,335] Assistance for Needy Families block grant.  

[6:5:66,353] 4260010 - CHILD SUPPORT ADMINISTRATION:  

[7:0:66,370] The Child Support Administration program provides funding for the salaries and benefits for local and state staff, and operating  

[7:1:66,380] expenses and equipment for the operation of California's child support program, including local child support agencies. The  

[7:2:66,391] federal government provides 66 percent of the funding and the state funds 34 percent of the administration costs.  

[7:3:66,408] 4260019 - CHILD SUPPORT AUTOMATION:  

[8:0:66,426] Pursuant to Federal law, the Department created a single, statewide child support automation system that meets federal  

[8:1:66,436] certification. There are two components of the statewide system: the Child Support Enforcement system and the State  

[8:2:66,446] Disbursement Unit. The enforcement system provides local child support staff tools to manage child support customer accounts  

[8:3:66,457] and locate and intercept assets of non-custodial parents delinquent in their child support payments. The Child Support  

[8:4:66,467] Automation program provides funding for the vendor-operated state disbursement unit, which collects child support payments  

[8:5:66,477] from non-custodial parents and disburses payments to custodial parties. In addition, the Child Support Automation program  

[8:6:66,487] provides funding for electronic data processing maintenance and operation costs at local agencies.

[15:0:66,573] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[15:1:65,593] • Child Support Payments—The Budget increases the amount of child support payments passed through to CalWORKs  

[15:2:76,603] families, effective January 1, 2022, from the current $50 to $100 for a family with one child and $200 for a family with two or  

[15:3:76,613] more children. This change is anticipated to result in an additional $34 million annually passed-through to approximately  

[15:4:76,623] 160,000 CalWORKs families, and reduce annual General Fund revenues by $17 million. The Budget includes $0.6 million  

[15:5:76,633] General Fund for the necessary automation changes needed to implement the proposal in 2021-22.  

[16:0:65,650] • CalFresh Application Assistance—The Budget includes $5 million General Fund annually to maintain the GetCalFresh.org  

[16:1:76,660] website, a statewide online application assistance tool that provides a streamlined application experience and allows clients  

[16:2:76,670] to apply on multiple platforms. The website will be maintained until a CalSAWS statewide portal becomes operational and  

[16:3:76,680] offers the same level of client service and language access.  

[17:0:65,696] • Food Banks—The Budget includes $50 million one-time General Fund for existing Emergency Food Assistance Program  

[17:1:76,707] providers, food banks, tribes, and tribal organizations to mitigate increases in food needs among low-income and food-

[18:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:76,83] insecure populations.  

[4:0:65,99] • CalFresh Simplifications—The Budget includes statutory changes that simplify CalFresh verification, reporting, and  

[4:1:76,109] interviewing processes, require DSS to develop a pre-populated semi-annual reporting form, and maximize integrated  

[4:2:76,119] application for CalFresh and Medi-Cal benefits.The Budget includes $27.5 million General Fund in 2020-21 and $8.4 million  

[4:3:76,130] annually thereafter for these purposes.  

[5:0:65,146] • CalWORKs Time Clocks—The Budget includes statutory changes to establish a single 60-month CalWORKs time limit and  

[5:1:76,156] allow clients to participate in a greater array of welfare-to-work activities for the entire 60 months, effective May 1, 2022 or  

[5:2:76,166] when automation is possible. The Budget includes $2.6 million General Fund/Temporary Assistance for Needy Families  

[5:3:76,176] (TANF) block grant funding in 2020-21, growing to $66.2 million General Fund in 2023-24.  

[6:0:65,193] • CalWORKs Single Allocation—The Budget includes $2.4 billion General Fund/TANF for counties’ CalWORKs Single  

[6:1:76,203] Allocation which funds employment services, county administration, Stage One child care, and Cal-Learn.  

[7:0:65,219] • CalWORKs Outcomes and Accountability Review (Cal-OAR)—The Budget includes statutory changes making Cal-OAR  

[7:1:76,229] activity optional for counties in 2020-21, resulting in a one-time reduction of $21 million General Fund/TANF.  

[8:0:65,245] • CalWORKs Home Visiting Program—The Budget includes a one-time reduction of $30 million General Fund/TANF and  

[8:1:76,256] continues to serve clients already enrolled in the CalWORKs Home Visiting program.  

[9:0:65,272] • Training for County Social Workers and Managers—The Budget includes $1.9 million General Fund in 2020-21 and  

[9:1:76,282] $120,000 General Fund ongoing to support additional training for county social workers and managers with respect to  

[9:2:76,292] conducting needs assessments for IHSS recipients to promote consistency across all counties with respect to program  

[9:3:76,302] requirements.  

[10:0:65,319] • Conform IHSS Residual Program to Timing of Medi-Cal Coverage—The Budget includes savings of $72.6 million General  

[10:1:76,329] Fund in 2020-21 ongoing due to conforming the IHSS Residual Program to timing of Medi-Cal coverage.  

[11:0:65,345] • County Administration—The Budget includes savings of $12.2 million ongoing to freeze IHSS county administration funding  

[11:1:76,355] at the 2019-20 level.  

[12:0:65,371] • California Newcomer Education and Well-Being Project—The Budget includes $15 million one-time Proposition 98 General  

[12:1:76,382] Fund for the California Newcomer Education and Well-Being Project (CalNEW) to assist school districts in improving refugee  

[12:2:76,392] and unaccompanied undocumented minors students' well-being, English-language proficiency, and academic performance.  

[12:3:76,402] The funding, which is available over three years, will also provide school-based supports to immigrant families to address  

[12:4:76,412] harms caused by the federal “public charge” rule.  

[13:0:65,428] • Temporary Extended Foster Care Flexibilities—The Budget includes $32 million one-time General Fund to temporarily  

[13:1:76,439] extend foster care support to youth who turn 21 while in extended foster care after April 17, 2020 through June 30, 2021,  

[13:2:76,449] and for any nonminor dependent who met eligibility requirements for the Extended Foster Care program and lost their  

[13:3:76,459] employment or has experienced a disruption in their education program resulting from COVID-19, and cannot otherwise  

[13:4:76,469] meet any of the participation requirements.  

[14:0:65,485] • Foster Care Emergency Assistance—The Budget includes $13.4 million one-time General Fund in 2020-21 to provide  

[14:1:76,496] caregivers with up to four months of emergency assistance payments pending resource family approval and up to twelve  

[14:2:76,506] months for cases that meet good cause criteria. Beginning in 2021-22 and annually thereafter, the state will fund up to three  

[14:3:76,516] months of emergency assistance payments for caregivers pending approval, as local child welfare agencies and probation  

[14:4:76,526] departments are anticipated to complete the resource family approval process on a timelier basis.  

[15:0:65,542] • Transitional Housing Supplement for Older Foster Youth—The Budget includes $4 million General Fund ongoing to provide a  

[15:1:76,553] transitional housing supplement for foster youth over 18 years of age.  

[16:0:65,569] • Continuum of Care Reform Reconciliation for Fiscal Years 2016-17 and 2017-18—The Budget includes $2.6 million one-time  

[16:1:76,579] General Fund in 2020-21 to reflect Continuum of Care Reform true-up related to county Child and Family Teams actual  

[16:2:76,589] expenditures for fiscal years 2016-17 and 2017-18 and $80 million one-time General Fund in 2020-21 to support county child  

[16:3:76,599] welfare departments.  

[17:0:65,616] • Community Care License: New Facility Management System for Certification, Approval, and Licensing—The Budget  

[17:1:76,626] includes $28.7 million General Fund for over three years beginning in 2020-21 to implement a Platform as a Service solution  

[17:2:76,636] for the Community Care Licensing Division.
