[0:0:66,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:407,13] 2020-21 STATE BUDGET — HHS   179 

[2:0:166,29] 5180   Department of Social Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,53] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:0:66,72] 4270 - WELFARE PROGRAMS  

[5:0:66,93] The Department's public assistance programs provide financial assistance to California residents who are unable to support  

[5:1:66,103] themselves. These programs are comprised of five components:  

[6:0:65,121] • California Work Opportunity and Responsibility to Kids (CalWORKs)  

[7:0:65,137] • Other Assistance Payments, including Foster Care, Adoption Assistance Program, Refugee Cash Assistance, and Food  

[7:1:76,147] Assistance Programs  

[8:0:65,163] • Supplemental Security Income/State Supplementary Payment Program  

[9:0:65,179] • County Administration and Automation Projects  

[10:0:65,196] • Disaster Relief  

[11:0:66,224] The objectives of these programs are to provide temporary financial assistance to eligible needy and dependent persons to  

[11:1:66,234] enable achievement of self-sufficiency or to provide safe living environments for vulnerable adults and children, and to monitor,  

[11:2:66,244] administer, and improve the quality of all welfare services.  

[12:0:66,262] 4270010 - CalWORKs:  

[13:0:66,279] The CalWORKs program is California's version of the federal Temporary Assistance for Needy Families program. CalWORKs is  

[13:1:66,290] California's largest cash aid program for children and families and is designed to provide temporary assistance to meet basic  

[13:2:66,300] needs, such as shelter, food, and clothing, in times of crisis, while encouraging personal responsibility. CalWORKs includes  

[13:3:66,310] specific welfare-to-work requirements and provides supportive services, such as child care, to enable an individual to meet  

[13:4:66,320] these requirements. Child care services currently are provided through a three-stage system to current and former CalWORKs  

[13:5:66,330] recipients with children through the age of 10 (or up to 12 under certain conditions). Stage One is administered by the  

[13:6:66,341] Department of Social Services. Stages Two and Three are administered by the California Department of Education. Parents  

[13:7:66,351] have the right to choose child care among center-based, family child care homes, or license-exempt providers. CalWORKs  

[13:8:66,361] families are then able to meet both goals of moving from welfare into the work force and engaging children in child care and  

[13:9:66,371] development services.  

[14:0:66,389] 4270019 - Other Assistance Payments:  

[15:0:66,407] The Foster Care program provides assistance payments to relatives, foster family homes, foster family agencies, short-term  

[15:1:66,417] residential treatment centers or group homes for children who have been removed from the custody of a parent or guardian as  

[15:2:66,427] a result of a judicial order or voluntary placement agreement due to findings of abuse, neglect or exploitation. This program is  

[15:3:66,437] administered by the counties in accordance with regulations, standards, and procedures set by the Department of Social  

[15:4:66,447] Services as authorized by federal and state law. The Kinship Guardianship Assistance Program provides support payments to  

[15:5:66,458] relative guardians of children who were previously in the foster care system.  

[16:0:66,475] The Adoption Assistance Program provides financial assistance to families adopting a child with special needs or to facilitate  

[16:1:66,485] the adoption of children who otherwise would remain in long-term foster care. This program is administered by the counties in  

[16:2:66,496] accordance with regulations, standards, and procedures set by the Department of Social Services as authorized by federal and  

[16:3:66,506] state law.  

[17:0:66,524] California also provides cash assistance to eligible refugee/entrant populations via the following programs:  

[18:0:65,541] • The Refugee Cash Assistance provides cash grants to refugees/entrants in their first eight months in the United States  

[18:1:76,551] provided they are not otherwise eligible for categorical welfare programs.  

[19:0:65,569] • The Unaccompanied Refugee Minors program provides culturally and linguistically appropriate child welfare, foster care, and  

[19:1:76,579] independent living services to minors who do not have parents in the United States, or who enter the United States  

[19:2:76,590] unaccompanied by a parent, an immediate adult relative, or an adult having documentable legal evidence of custody of the  

[19:3:76,600] minor.  

[20:0:65,617] • The Trafficking and Crime Victims Assistance Program provides cash aid and social services to noncitizen victims of human  

[20:1:76,628] trafficking, domestic violence and other serious crimes who meet the income and eligibility requirements. Benefits are  

[20:2:76,638] available for a maximum period of eight months for adults without children and up to 48 months for families (under  

[20:3:76,648] CalWORKs).  

[21:0:66,666] The CalFresh Program, federally referred to as the Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program, provides improved levels of  

[21:1:66,676] nutrition among eligible low-income households by offering them a benefit amount, posted to a debit card, for the purpose of  

[21:2:66,686] purchasing food. The cost of CalFresh benefits is provided by the United States Department of Agriculture for populations  

[21:3:66,696] eligible to receive federal benefits. Legal immigrants who meet program eligibility criteria but are ineligible for federal benefits  

[21:4:66,707] due to their immigration status are served under the state-funded program known as the California Food Assistance Program.  

[22:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

# === PAGE 182 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] 2020-21 STATE BUDGET — HHS   180 

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:166,29] 5180   Department of Social Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,83] The CalFresh Employment and Training Program requires certain non-assistance CalFresh recipients to participate in  

[3:1:66,93] employment and training activities.  

[4:0:66,111] The Emergency Food Assistance Program provides commodities to local food banks in all 58 California counties for distribution  

[4:1:66,121] to the working poor, low-income, unemployed, and homeless persons. The food is distributed to eligible recipients for  

[4:2:66,131] household consumption or used to prepare and serve meals in congregate settings. This program is also supplemented with  

[4:3:66,141] food purchased by food banks using private donations, funds provided by the state, taxpayer contributions generated through a  

[4:4:66,152] state income tax check-off, as well as surplus fresh fruits and vegetables donated by farmers and businesses.  

[5:0:66,169] The Commodity Supplemental Food Program is a federally funded program for local non-profit agencies to provide nutritious  

[5:1:66,179] supplemental foods to low-income, elderly people at least 60 years of age. Administrative responsibility for the Commodity  

[5:2:66,190] Supplemental Food Program was transferred from the California Department of Education to the Department of Social Services  

[5:3:66,200] on October 1, 2016.  

[6:0:66,218] 4270028 - Supplemental Security Income/State Supplementary Payment Program:  

[7:0:66,235] The federal Supplemental Security Income (SSI) program is a cash assistance program for low-income aged, blind, or disabled  

[7:1:66,245] persons who meet the program's income and resource requirements. California supplements the federal SSI payment with a  

[7:2:66,256] State Supplementary Payment (SSP). The SSI/SSP program is administered by the federal Social Security Administration who  

[7:3:66,266] determines eligibility, computes grants, and disburses the combined monthly payment to recipients.  

[8:0:66,284] 4270037 - County Administration and Automation Projects:  

[9:0:66,301] Federal, state, and county governments share the cost of operating expenses and the salaries and benefits of county staff who  

[9:1:66,311] administer public assistance programs.  

[10:0:66,329] Federal, state, and county funds are used to finance major data automation projects of the Department of Social Services.  

[11:0:66,347] 4270046 - Disaster Relief:  

[12:0:66,357] The objective of the Disaster Relief Program is to provide monetary assistance to individuals and households who have  

[12:1:66,367] suffered eligible losses from a Presidentially-declared disaster that are not covered by other federal, state, or private assistance  

[12:2:66,377] programs, and to oversee mass care and shelter, social services recovery, emergency repatriation, and administration of select  

[12:3:66,388] recovery grants.  

[13:0:66,405] 4275 - SOCIAL SERVICES AND LICENSING  

[14:0:66,423] The Department of Social Services oversees and monitors the administration of social services programs, which include child  

[14:1:66,433] welfare, adoptions, licensing and special programs. The department is responsible for development of policy, regulations, and  

[14:2:66,443] procedures that govern the delivery of services to children, families and other recipients, and the monitoring and evaluation of  

[14:3:66,454] the service delivery system.  

[15:0:66,471] 4275010 - In-Home Supportive Services:  

[16:0:66,489] The In-Home Supportive Services (IHSS) program provides in-home services that enable eligible individuals to remain safely in  

[16:1:66,499] their own homes as an alternative to out-of-home care. Eligible persons are low-income aged, blind, or disabled individuals who  

[16:2:66,509] either qualify for federally funded Medi-Cal or meet the program's income and resource requirements. There are four programs  

[16:3:66,520] that provide in-home care: the Personal Care Services Program, IHSS Plus Option Program, Community First Choice Option,  

[16:4:66,530] and IHSS-Residual Program.  

[17:0:66,548] 4275019 - Children and Adult Services and Licensing:  

[18:0:66,558] The Children's Services component consists of three major areas: Child Welfare Services, Adoptions, and Child Abuse  

[18:1:66,568] Prevention.  

[19:0:66,588] Child Welfare Services provides emergency response, family maintenance, family reunification, and permanent placement and  

[19:1:66,599] prevention services to protect abused, neglected or exploited children. The services are provided through an integrated  

[19:2:66,609] services delivery system that provides intensive services to families to promote child safety, permanency and well-being with  

[19:3:66,619] the goal of allowing families to stay together in their own homes, or arrangement for the child's placement in the safest and  

[19:4:66,629] least restrictive home-like setting. Services also include assistance to youth who are emancipating or have emancipated from  

[19:5:66,639] foster care. The program also provides training and technical assistance to county administrators and staff.  

[20:0:66,660] In Child Welfare Services, the Department of Social Services is implementing continuum of care reforms codified in Chapter  

[20:1:66,670] 773, Statutes of 2015. The reforms emphasize home-based family care, improve access to services without having to change  

[20:2:66,680] out-of-home placements to get those services, and increase the role of children, youth, and families in assessment and case  

[20:3:66,690] planning.  

[21:0:66,711] The Adoptions Program provides support services to children and adoptive families through a collaboration of public and  

[22:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:407,13] 2020-21 STATE BUDGET — HHS   181 

[2:0:166,29] 5180   Department of Social Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,83] private adoption agencies in the state. Agency adoptions provide adoption services through public and private agencies for  

[3:1:66,93] children who have been abused, neglected or exploited and are under the jurisdiction of the county or tribal court. Services  

[3:2:66,103] include adoptive placement screening; home studies; reimbursement of non-recurring adoption expenses for adoptive parents;  

[3:3:66,113] training, recruitment and retention of foster parents; and technical assistance and support for inter-country adoptions. For  

[3:4:66,124] independent adoptions, the public agency investigates a proposed adoption and provides a report to the court when the  

[3:5:66,134] biological parents place their children directly with adoptive parents of their choice.  

[4:0:66,154] The Child Abuse Prevention Program provides funding, training, and technical assistance for the development and  

[4:1:66,164] sustainability of child abuse prevention and early intervention programs, education and outreach materials, activities, and  

[4:2:66,175] services for at risk families and their children.  

[5:0:66,195] The Adult Protective Services program provides funding for counties to address reports of abuse, neglect, or financial  

[5:1:66,205] exploitation of elder or dependent adults and provide intervention, as necessary.  

[6:0:66,226] The Community Care Licensing Program is a regulatory enforcement program with the responsibility of protecting the health  

[6:1:66,236] and safety of children and adults residing in or spending a portion of their time in out-of-home care. The program includes  

[6:2:66,246] facility licensure, prevention, compliance, and enforcement components.  

[6:3:66,264] 4275028 - Special Programs:  

[7:0:66,281] The Special Programs provides funds for Foster Care Burial, Assistance Dog Special Allowance, Access Assistance to the  

[7:1:66,292] Deaf, Refugee Programs, Immigration and Naturalization Assistance Services and Legal Services for Unaccompanied and  

[7:2:66,302] Undocumented Minors.  

[7:3:66,320] 4280 - TITLE IV-E WAIVER  

[8:0:66,337] The Title IV-E California Child Well-Being Project is a federal waiver demonstration project in California. This project provides  

[8:1:66,347] participating counties with a capped federal grant that in turn provides flexibility in the use of federal and state foster care  

[8:2:66,358] maintenance and administrative funds on program and services expenditures that were previously unallowable.  

[8:3:66,375] 4285 - DISABILITY EVALUATION AND OTHER SERVICES  

[9:0:66,393] The objective of this program is to determine an applicant's medical and/or vocational eligibility for disability benefits and  

[9:1:66,403] provide administrative services to other agencies.  

[9:2:66,421] 4285010 - Disability Evaluation:  

[10:0:66,439] The Disability Evaluation Program determines the medical, vocational, and/or functional eligibility of California residents  

[10:1:66,449] applying for benefits under Title II (Disability Insurance), Title XVI (Supplemental Security Income), and Title XIX (Medicaid) of  

[10:2:66,459] the Social Security Act. Eligibility is determined by the severity of the individual's physical and/or mental impairment(s) and  

[10:3:66,469] overall ability to engage in substantial gainful employment.  

[10:4:66,487] 4285019 - Services to Other Agencies:  

[11:0:66,497] In addition to providing support services for its programs, the Department of Social Services provides general administrative  

[11:1:66,507] services, such as personnel and accounting to the State Council on Developmental Disabilities and the Health and Human  

[11:2:66,518] Services Agency. The Department provides services to the Medi-Cal Program in the form of state hearings and public  

[11:3:66,528] information services.  

[11:4:66,545] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION  

[12:0:66,563] The objective of the Administration program is to provide overall management, planning, policy development, and  

[12:1:66,573] administrative support services to other departmental programs.

[3:0:66,53] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:1:66,72] 4350 - STATE-LOCAL REALIGNMENT  

[4:0:66,93] The objectives of Realignment are to assign program responsibility to the most appropriate level of government and achieve  

[4:1:66,103] improved service levels with broad discretion given to the responsible entity. Realignment provides for greater funding stability  

[4:2:66,113] for selected programs, increased local flexibility in administering these programs, and productive fiscal incentives to encourage  

[4:3:66,123] cost-effective approaches to providing services.  

[5:0:66,144] Total Realignment revenues are comprised of a half cent sales tax and a dedicated portion of vehicle license fee revenues.  

[5:1:66,154] Revenues are deposited into the Local Revenue Fund, which includes several accounts. Funds deposited in these accounts  

[5:2:66,164] are continuously appropriated for allocation to local governments according to formula and are used to fund programs specified  

[5:3:66,174] in realignment legislation. The legislation also includes local maintenance of effort and matching requirements in order to  

[5:4:66,185] ensure that counties do not use the realigned funds to supplant local expenditure levels prior to realignment. This provision  

[5:5:66,195] ensures compliance with other state and federal statutes which, in turn, provide hundreds of millions of dollars annually for  

[5:6:66,205] county health and social services programs.  

[6:0:66,245] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM

[16:0:66,683] Building upon the 1991-92 Realignment, 2011 Realignment moves program and fiscal responsibility to counties, providing a  

[16:1:66,693] dedicated source of funding while eliminating duplication of effort, generating savings, and increasing flexibility.  

[17:0:66,714] Realigned programs include local public safety programs, mental health, substance abuse, foster care, child welfare services,

[3:0:66,83] and adult protective services. Many of these programs are already administered at the local level by counties. Therefore, it is  

[3:1:66,93] appropriate for the programmatic and fiscal responsibility to reside with the counties with the state maintaining an oversight and  

[3:2:66,103] technical assistance role where needed. These changes are made with the goal of providing services more efficiently and at  

[3:3:66,113] less cost.  

[3:4:66,134] The funding sources for realignment are:  

[3:5:65,152] • The dedication of 1.0625 cents of a state special fund sales tax.  

[3:6:65,168] • The dedication of a portion of vehicle license fee revenues.  

[4:0:66,196] Counties receive 2011 Realignment funding from the following accounts and their related growth accounts:  

[4:1:65,213] • Protective Services Subaccount (Foster Care, Child Welfare Services, and Adult Protective Services)  

[4:2:65,230] • Behavioral Health Subaccount (Early and Periodic Screening, Diagnosis, and Treatment; Mental Health Managed Care;  

[4:3:76,240] Substance Abuse Treatment; and Women and Children's Residential Treatment)

[5:3:65,331] • District Attorney and Public Defender Subaccount  

[6:0:65,347] • Juvenile Justice Subaccount (consisting of the Youthful Offender Block Grant Special Account and Juvenile Reentry Grant  

[6:1:76,357] Special Account)
